The Harm of Opposing Proven Science in the Name of Religion
Ghazali warns against opposing proven science in the name of religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali warns that opposing well-established scientific proofs in the name of religion causes more harm than the attacks of enemies.

Core Idea
An intelligent enemy is better than an ignorant friend.

Having introduced the second category, Ghazali now explains why it is dangerous to insist that such claims are against religion. He argues that when something is proven by clear geometrical and arithmetical reasoning, denying it only discredits the faith. This is one of the most quoted passages in the Tahafut, showing Ghazali's method of distinguishing between essential and non-essential doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's warning
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'وهذا الفن أيضاً لسنا نخوض فى إبطاله' and ends with 'عدو عاقل خير من صديق جاهل'. Notice the strong language.
Ghazali says whoever thinks refuting this is part of religion has 'committed aggression against religion'.
2
Understand the logic
The proof for eclipses is mathematical and leaves no doubt. If someone knows this proof and is told it contradicts religion, he will doubt religion, not the proof. So insisting on contradiction pushes people away from faith.
3
Grasp the metaphor
The saying 'an intelligent enemy is better than an ignorant friend' means that a misguided defender of religion does more damage than a clear opponent.
This is a key methodological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثانى : ما لا يصدم مذهبهم فيه أصلاً من أصول الدين ، وليس من ضرورة تصديق الأنبياء والرسل - صلوات الله عليهم - منازعتهم فيه ، كقولهم : إن الكسوف القمرى عبارة عن انمحاء ضوء القمر بتوسط الأرض بينه وبين الشمس ، من حيث إنه يقتبس نوره من الشمس ، والأرض كرة ، والسماء محيط بها من الجوانب ، فإذا وقع القمر في ظل الأرض ، انقطع عنه نور الشمس ؛ وكقولهم : إن كسوف الشمس معناه وقوع جرم القمر بين الناظر وبين الشمس ، وذلك عند اجتماعهما في العقدتين على دقيقة واحدة . وهذا الفن أيضاً لسنا نخوض فى إبطاله ، إذ لا يتعلق به غرض ، ومن ظن أن المناظرة في إبطال هذا من الدين ، فقد جنى على الدين وضعف أمره ، فإن هذه الأمور تقوم عليها براهين هندسية حسابية ، لا يبقى معها ريبة ، فمن يطلع عليها ، ويتحقق أدلتها ، حتى يخبر بسببها عن وقت الكسوفين ، وقدرهما ، ومدة بقائهما إلى الانجلاء ، إذا قيل له : إن هذا على خلاف الشرع ، لم يسترب فيه وإنما يسترب فى الشرع ، وضرر الشرع ممن ينصره لا بطريقه ، أكثر ضرره ممن يطعن فيه بطريق ه؛ وهو كما قيل : عدو عاقل خير من صديق جاهل . فإن قيل : فقد قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إن الشمس والقمر لآيتان من آيات الله ، لا يخسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته ، فإذا رأيتم ذلك فافزعوا إلى ذكر الله والصلاة ) ، فكيف يلائم هذا ما قالوه ؟ ، قلنا : وليس في هذا ما يناقض ما قالوه ، إذ ليس فيه إلا نفى وقوع الكسوف لموت أحد أو لحياته والأمر بالصلاة عنده ؛ والشرع الذي يأمر بالصلاة عند الزوال والغروب والطلوع ، من أين يبعد منه أن يأمر عند الكسوف بها استحباباً ؟ فإن قيل : فقد روى أنه قال فى آخر الحديث : « ولكن الله إذا تجلى لشيء خضع له » ، فيدل على أن الكسوف خضوع بسبب التجلى ؛ قلنا هذه الزدة لم يصح نقلها ، فيجب تكذيب ناقلها ؛ وإنما المروى ما ذكرناه ، كيف ولو كان صحيحاً ، لكان تأويله أهون من مكابرة أمور قطعية ، فكم من ظواهر أولت بالأدلة العقلية التي لا تنتهى فى الوضوح إلى هذا الحد . وأعظم ما يفرح به : ناصر الشرع ، بأن هذا وأمثاله على خلاف الشرع يصرح الملاحدة ، أن فيسهل عليه طريق إبطال الشرع ، إن كان شرطه أمثال ذلك . وهذا لأن البحث في العالم كونه حادثاً أو قديماً ، ثم إذا ثبت حدوثه فسواء كان كرة ، أو بسيطاً أو مسدساً ، أم مثمناً ؛ وسواء كانت السموات وما تحتها ثلاث عشرة طبقة - The second section: that which does not clash with their belief in any fundamental principle of religion, and disputing them in it is not necessary for the affirmation of prophets and messengers (peace of God upon them), such as their saying: lunar eclipse is the disappearance of the moon's light by the earth's interposition between it and the sun, since it derives its light from the sun, and the earth is a sphere, and the sky surrounds it from all sides, so when the moon falls into the earth's shadow, the sun's light is cut off from it; and their saying: solar eclipse means the moon's body falling between the observer and the sun, and that occurs when they meet at the two nodes on one precise minute. And this type we also do not delve into refuting it, for no purpose is attached to it, and whoever thinks that debating in refuting this is part of religion has committed aggression against religion and weakened its affair, for these matters are established by geometrical and arithmetical proofs concerning which no doubt remains. Whoever becomes acquainted with them and verifies their proofs, such that he can predict by means of them the time of the two eclipses, their magnitude, and their duration until clearing, if it is said to him: 'This is contrary to the Sharia,' he will not doubt it but will rather doubt the Sharia. And the harm to the Sharia from one who supports it not in its proper way is greater than the harm from one who attacks it in its own way; and it is as was said: an intelligent enemy is better than an ignorant friend. If it is said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed the sun and the moon are two signs from the signs of God, they are not eclipsed for anyone's death nor for anyone's life, so if you see that, hasten to the remembrance of God and prayer.' So how does this accord with what they say? We say: There is nothing in this that contradicts what they say, for it only contains the negation of the occurrence of eclipse for anyone's death or life, and the command to pray at it; and the Sharia that commands prayer at noon, sunset and sunrise, how far is it from commanding prayer at eclipse as a recommendation? If it is said: It was narrated that he said at the end of the hadith: 'But when God manifests to something, it becomes humbled,' indicating that eclipse is due to humbling because of manifestation. How many apparent meanings have been interpreted by rational proofs that do not reach this level of clarity? And the greatest thing that gladdens the supporter of the Sharia is that this and its like are declared by the atheists to be contrary to the Sharia, so that it becomes easy for him to invalidate the Sharia if its condition is such matters. This is because the investigation about the world is whether it is originated or eternal; then if its origination is established, it is the same whether it is a sphere, or flat, or hexagonal, or octagonal; and whether the heavens and what is beneath them are thirteen layers as they say, or fewer or more; so the proportion of investigating that to divine investigation is like the proportion of investigating the layers of an onion and their number and the number of pomegranate seeds; the point is only that it is an act of God, however it is.

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the second category of philosophical claims that do not clash with the fundamentals of religion and are not necessary for affirming prophethood. Ghazali gives the example of astronomical explanations of lunar and solar eclipses. He argues that these are established by geometrical and arithmetical proofs leaving no doubt, so trying to refute them as part of religion harms religion by making it appear false. He then addresses the hadith about the Prophet saying that the sun and moon are signs of God and are not eclipsed for anyone's death, and to pray when seeing them. Ghazali says there is no contradiction: the hadith only negates that eclipses occur for a person's death or life, and it commands prayer, which is in harmony with Sharia that commands prayers at other times. He dismisses an additional narration about God manifesting to things causing submission as inauthentic, and even if authentic, interpretation is easier than rejecting decisive proofs. He concludes that insisting such things contradict Sharia only gives atheists a way to attack religion. Then he generalizes: the important thing about the world is whether it is created or eternal; its specific shape or number of heavens is irrelevant to divine investigation, like studying the layers of an onion.

Key Terms
البراهين الهندسية الحسابية
الملاحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that to defend religion, one must refute all scientific claims that seem to contradict scripture.
Correction: Ghazali shows that if the science is proven, denying it only discredits religion; it is better to accept the science and reinterpret scripture if needed, or recognize that the claim is not religiously relevant.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what happens when a person who knows the astronomical proofs for eclipses is told that this contradicts the Sharia?
A) He will doubt the proofs
B) He will doubt the Sharia
C) He will abandon both
D) He will become a philosopher

Key Takeaway
Opposing well-established scientific proofs in the name of religion harms religion more than the attacks of its enemies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defended a religious position without fully understanding the opposing science or argument, and what damage might that have caused to someone's perception of Islam? Will you commit to seeking knowledge before defending?
?
Think of a time when you were more concerned about being 'right' in a religious debate than about the truth being established. How can you shift your priority to truth, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
?
If someone you love has been turned away from Islam because of a misguided defender of religion, how does that weigh on your heart? What concrete step will you take today to be a 'wise friend' rather than a 'dangerous ally'?

Causality and Created Things
advanced
7 min
Reconciling Hadith and Science on Eclipses
Ghazali reconciles the eclipse hadith with astronomy and dismisses a weak narration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali reconciles the prophetic hadith about eclipses with the astronomical explanation, and why he dismisses an additional narration as inauthentic.

Core Idea
The hadith does not contradict astronomy; it only negates superstitious beliefs.

Having established that astronomical explanations are established fact, Ghazali now faces potential objections from the hadith. The Prophet (SAW) said that the sun and moon are signs of God and are not eclipsed for anyone's death or life. Does this conflict with the scientific account? Ghazali answers with careful textual analysis and hermeneutical principles, showing that the hadith is compatible. He also rejects a weak addition to the hadith that might cause unnecessary tension.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Ghazali's response
Read the Arabic passage from 'فإن قيل' to 'استحباباً' . Notice the objection quotes the hadith, and Ghazali responds by clarifying its meaning.
The hadith negates eclipses being caused by human events, but does not negate natural causation.
2
Examine the additional narration
Read the part about the additional claim that the sun and moon become humble due to God's manifestation. Ghazali dismisses it as inauthentic.
Even if it were authentic, he says interpretation is easier than rejecting decisive proofs.
3
Understand the onion analogy
Read the concluding part comparing the world's shape to an onion's layers. This reinforces that only creation matters, not specific details.
This is a broader methodological point for all such claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثانى : ما لا يصدم مذهبهم فيه أصلاً من أصول الدين ، وليس من ضرورة تصديق الأنبياء والرسل - صلوات الله عليهم - منازعتهم فيه ، كقولهم : إن الكسوف القمرى عبارة عن انمحاء ضوء القمر بتوسط الأرض بينه وبين الشمس ، من حيث إنه يقتبس نوره من الشمس ، والأرض كرة ، والسماء محيط بها من الجوانب ، فإذا وقع القمر في ظل الأرض ، انقطع عنه نور الشمس ؛ وكقولهم : إن كسوف الشمس معناه وقوع جرم القمر بين الناظر وبين الشمس ، وذلك عند اجتماعهما في العقدتين على دقيقة واحدة . وهذا الفن أيضاً لسنا نخوض فى إبطاله ، إذ لا يتعلق به غرض ، ومن ظن أن المناظرة في إبطال هذا من الدين ، فقد جنى على الدين وضعف أمره ، فإن هذه الأمور تقوم عليها براهين هندسية حسابية ، لا يبقى معها ريبة ، فمن يطلع عليها ، ويتحقق أدلتها ، حتى يخبر بسببها عن وقت الكسوفين ، وقدرهما ، ومدة بقائهما إلى الانجلاء ، إذا قيل له : إن هذا على خلاف الشرع ، لم يسترب فيه وإنما يسترب فى الشرع ، وضرر الشرع ممن ينصره لا بطريقه ، أكثر ضرره ممن يطعن فيه بطريق ه؛ وهو كما قيل : عدو عاقل خير من صديق جاهل . فإن قيل : فقد قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إن الشمس والقمر لآيتان من آيات الله ، لا يخسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته ، فإذا رأيتم ذلك فافزعوا إلى ذكر الله والصلاة ) ، فكيف يلائم هذا ما قالوه ؟ ، قلنا : وليس في هذا ما يناقض ما قالوه ، إذ ليس فيه إلا نفى وقوع الكسوف لموت أحد أو لحياته والأمر بالصلاة عنده ؛ والشرع الذي يأمر بالصلاة عند الزوال والغروب والطلوع ، من أين يبعد منه أن يأمر عند الكسوف بها استحباباً ؟ فإن قيل : فقد روى أنه قال فى آخر الحديث : « ولكن الله إذا تجلى لشيء خضع له » ، فيدل على أن الكسوف خضوع بسبب التجلى ؛ قلنا هذه الزدة لم يصح نقلها ، فيجب تكذيب ناقلها ؛ وإنما المروى ما ذكرناه ، كيف ولو كان صحيحاً ، لكان تأويله أهون من مكابرة أمور قطعية ، فكم من ظواهر أولت بالأدلة العقلية التي لا تنتهى فى الوضوح إلى هذا الحد . وأعظم ما يفرح به : ناصر الشرع ، بأن هذا وأمثاله على خلاف الشرع يصرح الملاحدة ، أن فيسهل عليه طريق إبطال الشرع ، إن كان شرطه أمثال ذلك . وهذا لأن البحث في العالم كونه حادثاً أو قديماً ، ثم إذا ثبت حدوثه فسواء كان كرة ، أو بسيطاً أو مسدساً ، أم مثمناً ؛ وسواء كانت السموات وما تحتها ثلاث عشرة طبقة - كما قالوه - أو أقل أو أكثر ؛ فنسبة النظر فيه إلى البحث الإلهى ، كنسبة النظر فى طبقات البصلة وعددها وعدد حب الرمان ؛ فالمقصود كونه من فعل الله فقط كيفما كان
The second section: that which does not clash with their belief in any fundamental principle of religion, and disputing them in it is not necessary for the affirmation of prophets and messengers (peace of God upon them), such as their saying: lunar eclipse is the disappearance of the moon's light by the earth's interposition between it and the sun, since it derives its light from the sun, and the earth is a sphere, and the sky surrounds it from all sides, so when the moon falls into the earth's shadow, the sun's light is cut off from it; and their saying: solar eclipse means the moon's body falling between the observer and the sun, and that occurs when they meet at the two nodes on one precise minute. And this type we also do not delve into refuting it, for no purpose is attached to it, and whoever thinks that debating in refuting this is part of religion has committed aggression against religion and weakened its affair, for these matters are established by geometrical and arithmetical proofs concerning which no doubt remains. Whoever becomes acquainted with them and verifies their proofs, such that he can predict by means of them the time of the two eclipses, their magnitude, and their duration until clearing, if it is said to him: 'This is contrary to the Sharia,' he will not doubt it but will rather doubt the Sharia. And the harm to the Sharia from one who supports it not in its proper way is greater than the harm from one who attacks it in its own way; and it is as was said: an intelligent enemy is better than an ignorant friend. If it is said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed the sun and the moon are two signs from the signs of God, they are not eclipsed for anyone's death nor for anyone's life, so if you see that, hasten to the remembrance of God and prayer.' So how does this accord with what they say? We say: There is nothing in this that contradicts what they say, for it only contains the negation of the occurrence of eclipse for anyone's death or life, and the command to pray at it; and the Sharia that commands prayer at noon, sunset and sunrise, how far is it from commanding prayer at eclipse as a recommendation? If it is said: It was narrated that he said at the end of the hadith: 'But when God manifests to something, it becomes humbled,' indicating that eclipse is due to humbling because of manifestation. We say: This addition was not authentically transmitted, so its transmitter must be declared a liar; rather what is narrated is what we mentioned. Even if it were authentic, its interpretation would be easier than obstinately rejecting decisive matters. How many apparent meanings have been interpreted by rational proofs that do not reach this level of clarity? And the greatest thing that gladdens the supporter of the Sharia is that this and its like are declared by the atheists to be contrary to the Sharia, so that it becomes easy for him to invalidate the Sharia if its condition is such matters. This is because the investigation about the world is whether it is originated or eternal; then if its origination is established, it is the same whether it is a sphere, or flat, or hexagonal, or octagonal; and whether the heavens and what is beneath them are thirteen layers as they say, or fewer or more; so the proportion of investigating that to divine investigation is like the proportion of investigating the layers of an onion and their number and the number of pomegranate seeds; the point is only that it is an act of God, however it is.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the second category of philosophical claims that do not clash with the fundamentals of religion and are not necessary for affirming prophethood. Ghazali gives the example of astronomical explanations of lunar and solar eclipses. He argues that these are established by geometrical and arithmetical proofs leaving no doubt, so trying to refute them as part of religion harms religion by making it appear false. He then addresses the hadith about the Prophet saying that the sun and moon are signs of God and are not eclipsed for anyone's death, and to pray when seeing them. Ghazali says there is no contradiction: the hadith only negates that eclipses occur for a person's death or life, and it commands prayer, which is in harmony with Sharia that commands prayers at other times. He dismisses an additional narration about God manifesting to things causing submission as inauthentic, and even if authentic, interpretation is easier than rejecting decisive proofs. He concludes that insisting such things contradict Sharia only gives atheists a way to attack religion. Then he generalizes: the important thing about the world is whether it is created or eternal; its specific shape or number of heavens is irrelevant to divine investigation, like studying the layers of an onion.

الحديث
التجلى
الظواهر
البراهين العقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith directly contradicts the astronomical explanation and that accepting science means rejecting the hadith.
Correction: Ghazali shows the hadith does not deny natural causation; it only denies that eclipses are caused by human events. The two are compatible.

Checkpoint
How does Ghazali respond to the objection that the Prophet's hadith about eclipses contradicts the astronomical explanation?
A) He says the hadith is not authentic
B) He says the hadith only negates superstitious causation, not natural causation
C) He says the astronomical explanation is false
D) He says the hadith must be interpreted allegorically

Key Takeaway
The hadith about eclipses is compatible with astronomy; authentic texts should be interpreted in light of certain proofs, and weak narrations should be rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a scientific fact that seems to conflict with a hadith you believe in, do you immediately assume the hadith is wrong or that science is wrong? Or do you pause to examine what the hadith actually says and what it does not say? This lesson shows that the Prophet's words only negated superstition. Are there hadith or verses you have misread because you assumed they said more than they do? Will you commit to reading the texts carefully before concluding there is a contradiction?
?
Ghazali rejects a weak narration even though it might support a pious viewpoint (that eclipses are due to God's manifestation). Are you willing to reject a 'nice' or emotionally appealing narration if it is not authentic? What attachments to weak narrations have you held onto because they felt spiritual? Today, will you resolve to only build your faith on authentic sources, even if they are less dramatic?
?
The lesson ends by saying that investigating whether the heavens are thirteen layers or fewer is like counting the layers of an onion; the only point is that it is an act of God. How much of your time and emotional energy is spent on debating secondary details of religion (like shape of the earth, number of heavens) while neglecting the core reality that everything is God's creation? What is one such detail you need to let go of in order to focus on what truly matters: your relationship with the Creator?

Ghazali's Method and Classification of Arguments
Ghazali presents his methodology and classification of the philosophers' arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali selects only certain arguments from the philosophers and how he classifies them into three types.

Core Idea
Ghazali filters arguments to those that truly challenge top scholars.

In this opening passage, Ghazali explains his approach to presenting the philosophers' proofs. He will not waste time on weak or arbitrary arguments, but instead focuses on those that can genuinely cause doubt for the most skilled theoreticians. He then states that the arguments are of three types, setting the stage for the detailed discussion.

Guided Path
1
Understand Ghazali's selection criteria
Read the first few lines where Ghazali states he will omit weak arguments and focus on those with impact. Note his phrases 'تحكم' and 'تخيل ضعيف'.
Ghazali's goal is to present the strongest case for the philosophers.
2
Identify the three types
Ghazali says 'وهذا الفن من الأدلة ثلاثة' (This kind of argument is of three types). Recognize that he is about to list them, but in this passage only the first is given.
The classification is a key structural element.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why Ghazali takes this approach. How does it strengthen his own refutation later?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيراد أدلتهم : لو ذهبت أصف ما نقل عنهم في معرض الأدلة، وذكر في الاعتراض عليه، لسوّدت في هذه المسألة أوراقا، ولكن لا خير في التطويل فلنحذف من أدلتهم، ما يجرى مجرى التحكم، أو التخيل الضعيف، الذي يهون على كل ناظر حله، ولنقتصر على إيراد ما له وقع في النفس، مما يجوز أن ينهض مشككاً لفحول النظار، فإن تشكيك الضعفاء بأدنى خيال ممكن. وهذا الفن من الأدلة ثلاثة :.

الأول: قولهم يستحيل صدور حادث من قديم مطلقاً، لأنا إذا فرضنا القديم ولم يصدر منه العالم مثلا، فإنما لم يصدر لأنه لم يكن للوجود مرجح، بل كان وجود العالم ممكناً إمكاناً صرفاً، فإذا حدث بعد ذلك لم يخل، إما أن يتجدد مرجح، أو لم يتجدد؛ فإن لم يتجدد مرجح، بقى العالم على الإمكان الصرف، كما كان قبل ذلك؛ وإن تجدد مرجح فمن محدث ذلك المرجح؟، ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث من قبل؟، والسؤال في حدوث المرجح قائم. بالجملة فأحوال القديم إذا كانت متشابهة، فإما أن لا يوجد عنه شيء يوجد على الدوام، وإما أن يتميز حال الترك عن حال الشروع وقط، وإما أن [؟] فهو محال. وتحقيقه أن يقال : لم لم يحدث العالم قبل حدوثه؟، لا يمكن أن يحال على عجزه عن الأحداث، ولا على استحالة الحدوث، فإن ذلك يؤدى إلى أن ينقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة، والعالم من الاستحالة إلى الإمكان، وكلاهما محالان، ولا يمكن أن يقال : لم يكن قبله غرض ثم تجدد غرض، ولا يمكن أن يحال على فقد آلة ثم على وجودها، بل أقرب ما يتخيل أن يقال : لم يرد وجوده قبل ذلك؛ فيلزم أن يقال : حصل وجوده لأنه صار مريداً لوجوده.
The presentation of their arguments: If I attempted to describe what has been transmitted from them in the way of arguments and mentioned [what has been said] in objection to them, I would blacken pages on this issue, but there is no good in prolixity. So we shall omit from their arguments what runs in the manner of arbitrary judgment or weak fancy, the refutation of which is easy for every examiner, and we shall restrict ourselves to presenting what has impact on the soul, such that it may serve as a cause of doubt for the top-tier of theoreticians, for causing doubt in the weak is possible with the slightest fancy. This kind of argument is of three types:

The first: Their statement: It is impossible for a temporal event to emanate from an eternal being absolutely, because if we assume the eternal and the world, for example, did not emanate from Him, then it did not emanate only because there was no preponderating factor for existence; rather the existence of the world was sheer possibility. Then when it occurred after that, it is inevitable: either a preponderating factor occurs anew, or it does not. If no preponderating factor occurs anew, then the world remains in sheer possibility, as it was before. And if a preponderating factor occurs anew, then who originated that preponderating factor? And why did it occur now and not before? The question regarding the temporal origination of the preponderating factor remains. In sum, if the states of the eternal are similar, then either nothing emanates from Him, or something emanates perpetually, or there is a distinction between the state of leaving and the state of beginning, or [؟] then it is impossible. And its verification is to say: Why did the world not occur before its occurrence? It cannot be attributed to His inability to create events, nor to the impossibility of occurrence, for that would lead to the eternal changing from inability to power, and the world from impossibility to possibility, both of which are impossible. Nor can it be said that there was no purpose before and then a purpose occurred anew. Nor can it be attributed to the absence of an instrument and then its existence. Rather, the closest thing one can imagine is to say: He did not will its existence before; then it follows that its existence occurred because He became willing of its existence.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the philosophers' arguments by Imam Ghazali, followed by the first of three types of proofs. Ghazali begins by stating he will not recount every argument due to prolixity but will select those that can genuinely cause doubt for serious scholars. He then introduces the classification: this type of argument is threefold. The first argument is the philosophers' claim that a temporal event cannot originate from an eternal being without an intermediary. The reasoning is as follows: if we assume the eternal (God) with no world emanating from Him, the world's existence was merely possible. When it later occurs, either a new preponderating factor emerges or not. If not, the world remains mere possibility. If a new factor emerges, that factor itself is temporal and raises the same question of why it occurred now and not before, leading to an infinite regress. Thus, if the eternal's states are all alike, either nothing emanates (so the world never exists) or something emanates perpetually (so the world always exists). Any temporal emergence would require a change in the eternal, which is impossible. Ghazali then provides a verification (tahqiq): Why did the world not occur earlier? It cannot be due to God's inability or the impossibility of the world's occurrence, as that would imply change in God. Nor can it be due to a new purpose or instrument, as that would also imply change. The only remaining explanation is a new will, but that would mean God became willing after not being willing, implying change. Hence, the argument concludes that temporal origination from an eternal being is impossible.

Key Terms
إيراد أدلتهم
تحكم
تخيل
فحول النظار
أدلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Ghazali omit certain arguments from the philosophers?
A) They are too difficult to explain.
B) They are arbitrary or weak fancies that are easy to refute.
C) He doesn't have enough space.
D) He wants to misrepresent the philosophers.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's approach is to present only the most challenging philosophers' arguments to make his own refutation more meaningful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter objections to your beliefs, do you tend to dismiss them as weak or do you honestly seek out the strongest ones, as Ghazali did? What would change if you confronted the most challenging doubts head-on?
?
Are there areas of your faith where you rely on 'arbitrary judgment' or 'weak fancy' rather than sound reasoning? Will you commit today to examining even the hardest questions that trouble the top scholars?

Causality and Created Things
advanced
8 min
First Argument: Temporal Events Cannot Originate from an Eternal Being
Ghazali presents the first philosophers' argument against temporal creation from an eternal being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the philosophers' first argument that a temporal event cannot emanate from an eternal being, including the key concept of a preponderating factor and the infinite regress problem.

Core Idea
If God is eternal and unchanging, why did He create the world at a specific time?

This argument is the first and one of the most powerful presented by the philosophers. It challenges the idea of a temporal creation by an eternal God. The reasoning goes: if God is eternal and all His attributes are the same, then He should either always create or never create. A temporal creation requires a new factor to tip the scales, but that factor itself would be temporal, leading to an infinite regress. Ghazali presents this argument in detail, then subjects it to a rigorous logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'الأول: قولهم' to the end. Follow the logical progression: assumption of no world, then the two alternatives.
Pay attention to the terms 'مرجح' (preponderating factor) and 'إمكان صرف' (sheer possibility).
2
Analyze the two alternatives
The argument considers whether a new preponderating factor arises or not. If not, the world remains merely possible. If yes, that factor itself is temporal and raises the same question – leading to infinite regress.
This is the core of the argument.
3
Study the verification (tahqiq)
Ghazali then examines four possible explanations for why the world did not occur earlier: inability, impossibility, absence of purpose, absence of instrument. He dismisses each because they would imply change in God.
The only remaining explanation is a new will, but that also implies change.
4
Understand the conclusion
The argument concludes that temporal origination from an eternal being is impossible. Recognize that this is presented as an objection to the Islamic view of creation.
Later, Ghazali will refute this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيراد أدلتهم : لو ذهبت أصف ما نقل عنهم في معرض الأدلة، وذكر في الاعتراض عليه، لسوّدت في هذه المسألة أوراقا، ولكن لا خير في التطويل فلنحذف من أدلتهم، ما يجرى مجرى التحكم، أو التخيل الضعيف، الذي يهون على كل ناظر حله، ولنقتصر على إيراد ما له وقع في النفس، مما يجوز أن ينهض مشككاً لفحول النظار، فإن تشكيك الضعفاء بأدنى خيال ممكن. وهذا الفن من الأدلة ثلاثة :.

الأول: قولهم يستحيل صدور حادث من قديم مطلقاً، لأنا إذا فرضنا القديم ولم يصدر منه العالم مثلا، فإنما لم يصدر لأنه لم يكن للوجود مرجح، بل كان وجود العالم ممكناً إمكاناً صرفاً، فإذا حدث بعد ذلك لم يخل، إما أن يتجدد مرجح، أو لم يتجدد؛ فإن لم يتجدد مرجح، بقى العالم على الإمكان الصرف، كما كان قبل ذلك؛ وإن تجدد مرجح فمن محدث ذلك المرجح؟، ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث من قبل؟، والسؤال في حدوث المرجح قائم. بالجملة فأحوال القديم إذا كانت متشابهة، فإما أن لا يوجد عنه شيء يوجد على الدوام، وإما أن يتميز حال الترك عن حال الشروع وقط، وإما أن [؟] فهو محال. وتحقيقه أن يقال : لم لم يحدث العالم قبل حدوثه؟، لا يمكن أن يحال على عجزه عن الأحداث، ولا على استحالة الحدوث، فإن ذلك يؤدى إلى أن ينقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة، والعالم من الاستحالة إلى الإمكان، وكلاهما محالان، ولا يمكن أن يقال : لم يكن قبله غرض ثم تجدد غرض، ولا يمكن أن يحال على فقد آلة ثم على وجودها، بل أقرب ما يتخيل أن يقال : لم يرد وجوده قبل ذلك؛ فيلزم أن يقال : حصل وجوده لأنه صار مريداً لوجوده.
The presentation of their arguments: If I attempted to describe what has been transmitted from them in the way of arguments and mentioned [what has been said] in objection to them, I would blacken pages on this issue, but there is no good in prolixity. So we shall omit from their arguments what runs in the manner of arbitrary judgment or weak fancy, the refutation of which is easy for every examiner, and we shall restrict ourselves to presenting what has impact on the soul, such that it may serve as a cause of doubt for the top-tier of theoreticians, for causing doubt in the weak is possible with the slightest fancy. This kind of argument is of three types:

The first: Their statement: It is impossible for a temporal event to emanate from an eternal being absolutely, because if we assume the eternal and the world, for example, did not emanate from Him, then it did not emanate only because there was no preponderating factor for existence; rather the existence of the world was sheer possibility. Then when it occurred after that, it is inevitable: either a preponderating factor occurs anew, or it does not. If no preponderating factor occurs anew, then the world remains in sheer possibility, as it was before. And if a preponderating factor occurs anew, then who originated that preponderating factor? And why did it occur now and not before? The question regarding the temporal origination of the preponderating factor remains. In sum, if the states of the eternal are similar, then either nothing emanates from Him, or something emanates perpetually, or there is a distinction between the state of leaving and the state of beginning, or [؟] then it is impossible. And its verification is to say: Why did the world not occur before its occurrence? It cannot be attributed to His inability to create events, nor to the impossibility of occurrence, for that would lead to the eternal changing from inability to power, and the world from impossibility to possibility, both of which are impossible. Nor can it be said that there was no purpose before and then a purpose occurred anew. Nor can it be attributed to the absence of an instrument and then its existence. Rather, the closest thing one can imagine is to say: He did not will its existence before; then it follows that its existence occurred because He became willing of its existence.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of the philosophers' arguments by Imam Ghazali, followed by the first of three types of proofs. Ghazali begins by stating he will not recount every argument due to prolixity but will select those that can genuinely cause doubt for serious scholars. He then introduces the classification: this type of argument is threefold. The first argument is the philosophers' claim that a temporal event cannot originate from an eternal being without an intermediary. The reasoning is as follows: if we assume the eternal (God) with no world emanating from Him, the world's existence was merely possible. When it later occurs, either a new preponderating factor emerges or not. If not, the world remains mere possibility. If a new factor emerges, that factor itself is temporal and raises the same question of why it occurred now and not before, leading to an infinite regress. Thus, if the eternal's states are all alike, either nothing emanates (so the world never exists) or something emanates perpetually (so the world always exists). Any temporal emergence would require a change in the eternal, which is impossible. Ghazali then provides a verification (tahqiq): Why did the world not occur earlier? It cannot be due to God's inability or the impossibility of the world's occurrence, as that would imply change in God. Nor can it be due to a new purpose or instrument, as that would also imply change. The only remaining explanation is a new will, but that would mean God became willing after not being willing, implying change. Hence, the argument concludes that temporal origination from an eternal being is impossible.

مرجح
إمكان صرف
استحالة
عجز
قدرة
غرض
آلة
إرادة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is Ghazali's own position or that he agrees with it.
Correction: Ghazali is presenting the philosophers' argument for the purpose of refuting it later. He does not endorse it.

Checkpoint
What happens according to the argument if no new preponderating factor arises when the world comes into existence?
A) The world comes into existence by itself.
B) The world remains in sheer possibility as before.
C) God creates the world without a reason.
D) The argument does not consider this case.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that a temporal event cannot originate from an eternal being because any such origination would require a change in the eternal, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's essence cannot change, how does this argument challenge your belief that God created the world at a specific time? Are you willing to reconsider your understanding of God's relationship to time?
?
You often pray for specific outcomes, acting as if God's will can be swayed by your requests. Does this argument force you to confront whether you truly believe in an unchanging God? What would it mean for your prayer life if God's will is eternal and immutable?
?
The philosophers claim that a new will in God would imply change. Do you ever treat God's actions as if they are reactions to human events? How might this argument lead you to a deeper trust in God's eternal decree, even when you don't understand His timing?

The Determining Factor Dilemma
Al-Ghazali presents the first dilemma of the murajjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's first dilemma: if a determining factor (murajjih) arises for the world's creation, it itself requires an originator, leading to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
A temporal event from the eternal demands a change; but that change must be explained.

Al-Ghazali begins by exposing the philosophers' claim that a temporal event cannot emanate from the eternal. He then presents a dilemma: either no determining factor arises, leaving the world in pure possibility, or a determining factor arises, which then itself requires an originator. This lesson unpacks the first part of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how al-Ghazali sets up the conditional: if no murajjih, nothing happens; if a murajjih arises, we ask about its source.
The phrase 'بالجملة' (in sum) signals the conclusion of this part.
2
Identify the two branches of the dilemma
The passage presents two possibilities: either no new determining factor arises, or one does. Trace each branch and its implication.
3
Reflect on the infinite regress
Notice that if a murajjih arises, the question 'who originated it?' applies to it as well, leading to an infinite chain. This is the core of the refutation.
This is a classic kalam argument against the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول قولهم يستحيل صدور حادث من قديم مطلقاً ، لأنا إذا فرضنا القديم ولم يصدر منه العالم مثلا ، فإنما لم يصدر لأنه لم يكن للوجود مرجح ، بل كان وجود العالم ممكناً إمكاناً صرفاً ، فإذا حدث بعد ذلك لم يخل ، إما أن يتجدد مرجح ، أو لم يتجدد ؛ فإن لم يتجدد مرجح ، بقى العالم على الإمكان الصرف ، كما كان قبل ذلك ؛ وإن تجدد مرجح فمن محدث ذلك المرجح ؟ ، ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث من قبل ؟ ، والسؤال في حدوث المرجح قائم . بالجملة فأحوال القديم إذا كانت متشابهة ، فإما أن لا يوجد عنه شيء يوجد على الدوام ، فأما أن يتميز حال الترك عن حال الشروع وقط ، وإما أن فهو محال • وتحقيقه أن يقال : لم لم يحدث العالم قبل حدوثه ؟ ، لا يمكن أن يحال على عجزه عن الأحداث ، ولا على استحالة الحدوث ، فإن ذلك يؤدى إلى أن ينقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة ، والعالم من الاستحالة إلى الإمكان ، وكلاهما محالان ، ولا يمكن أن يقال : لم يكن قبله غرض ثم تجدد غرض ولا يمكن أن يحال على فقد آلة ثم على وجودها ، بل أقرب ما يتخيل أن يقال : لم يرد وجوده قبل ذلك ؛ فيلزم أن يقال : حصل وجوده لأنه صار مريداً لوجوده بعد أن لم يكن مريداً ، فتكون قد حدثت الإرادة ، وحدوثه في ذاته محال ، لأنه ليس محل الحوادث ، وحدوثه لا في ذاته لا يجعله مريداً ولنترك النظر في محل حدوثه ، أليس الإشكال قائماً في أصل حدوثه ؟ ! وأنه من ؟! أين حدث ؟ ! ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبله ؟ ! أحدث الآن لا من جهة الله ؟ ! فإن جاز حادث من غير محدث ، فليكن العالم حادثاً لا صانع له ، وإلا فأى فرق بين حادث وحادث ؟ ! و إن حدث بإحداث الله ، فلم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبل ؟ ! ألعدم آلة ، أو قدرة ، أو غرض ، أو طبيعة . فلما أن تبدل ذلك بالوجود حدث ؟ ! عاد الإشكال بعينه . أو لعدم الإرادة ؟ ! فتفتقر الإرادة إلى إرادة وكذا الإرادة الأولى ، ويتسلسل إلى غير نهاية . فإذن قد تحقق بالقول المطلق أن صدور الحادث من القديم من غير تغير أمر من القديم في قدرة أو آلة أو وقت أو غرض، أو طبع ؛ محال ، وتقدير تغير حال محال ، لأن الكلام فى ذلك التغير الحادث كالكلام في غيره تنبيه : فما أقبح ما يقال : من أن الأمور العالية ، تحاول أن تفعل شيئاً لما تحتها لأن ذلك أحسن بها ، ولتكون فعالة للجميل ، أو أن الأول الحق يفعل شيئاً لأجل شيء ، وأن لفعله لمية .
The first [argument]: Their saying that it is impossible for a temporal event to proceed from the eternal at all. For if we suppose the eternal and the world, for example, did not proceed from it, then it did not proceed only because there was no determining factor (murajjih) for existence, rather the world's existence was pure possibility. Then when it occurred afterwards, it cannot be but that either a determining factor arises or does not arise. If no determining factor arises, the world remains in pure possibility as it was before. If a determining factor arises, then who originated that determining factor? And why did it occur now and not before? The question about the occurrence of the determining factor remains. In sum, if the states of the eternal are similar, then either nothing proceeds from it at all, or it proceeds perpetually. But distinguishing between the state of non-occurrence and the state of initiation is impossible. Its verification is to say: Why did the world not occur before its occurrence? It cannot be attributed to His inability to originate, nor to the impossibility of occurrence, for that would lead to the eternal changing from incapacity to power, and the world from impossibility to possibility, both of which are impossible. Nor can it be said that there was no purpose before and then a purpose arose, nor can it be attributed to the lack of an instrument and then its existence. Rather, the closest thing one might imagine is to say: He did not will its existence before. Then it necessarily follows that its existence occurred because He became willing of its existence after not being willing, so that the will (irada) would have occurred. Its occurrence in His essence is impossible because He is not a locus for temporal events, and its occurrence not in His essence does not make Him willing. Let us leave aside the consideration of its locus; is the problem not established in the very occurrence of the will? And from whom? Where did it occur? Why did it occur now and not before? Did it occur now from no direction of God? For if a temporal event is possible without an originator, then let the world be temporal without a Maker; else what difference is there between one temporal event and another? And if it occurs by God's causing-to-occur, why did it occur now and not before? Was it due to the absence of an instrument, or power, or purpose, or nature? When that changed to existence, it occurred? The same problem returns. Or due to the absence of will? Then the will would require another will, and so the first will, ad infinitum. So it is established absolutely that the emanation of a temporal event from the eternal without a change in the eternal in power, or instrument, or time, or purpose, or nature is impossible, and the assumption of a change in state is impossible, because the discussion about that temporal change is like the discussion about other than it. A reminder: How ugly it is to say that the lofty things try to do something for the sake of what is below them because that is better for them and so that they may be doers of the beautiful, or that the First Truth does something for the sake of something, and that His act has a 'why'.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by Imam al-Ghazali of the philosophers' claim that a temporal event (hadith) cannot emanate from an eternal being (qadim) at all. Al-Ghazali begins by presenting the core of their argument: if we suppose the eternal (God) and the world did not proceed from Him, then the world's existence was purely possible (imkan mahd) with no determining factor (murajjih). If later the world comes into existence, either a determining factor arises or it does not. If it does not arise, the world would remain in pure possibility, so no existence. If a determining factor does arise, then we ask: what originated that determining factor? And why now and not before? The same question applies to the determining factor itself, leading to an infinite regress. This is the first dilemma. Al-Ghazali then sharpens the argument: if the eternal's states are all similar (i.e., no change in essence or attributes), then either nothing proceeds from Him ever, or something proceeds perpetually—but distinguishing a moment of creation from a prior state of non-creation would imply a change in the eternal, which is impossible. He then deepens the analysis by asking why the world did not occur earlier. It cannot be due to God's inability (for that would imply change from incapacity to power) nor due to the impossibility of the world's existence (for that would imply a change from impossibility to possibility). Both are absurd. Nor can it be attributed to a new purpose or instrument arising in God, for that too implies change. The only plausible response is that God did not will the world's existence before. But then we ask: was His will eternal or temporal? If temporal, then the will itself is a temporal event that needs an originator—leading to an infinite regress of wills. If eternal, then the world should have existed eternally, contradicting its temporality. Al-Ghazali then makes a crucial point: if a temporal event can occur without an originator, then the world itself could be temporal without a Maker—which the philosophers deny. But if the world occurs by God's causing-to-occur (ihdath), then why now and not earlier? If due to the absence of an instrument, power, purpose, or nature, then when those are supplied, the same problem returns. If due to the absence of will, then will requires another will ad infinitum. Thus, the philosophers' position leads to an infinite regress or to change in the eternal—both impossible. The passage concludes with a warning against misguided justifications that say the lofty (i.e., God) acts for the sake of something else, or that His act has a 'why', which compromises divine transcendence. This is a classic kalam argument for the necessity of a temporal creation by an eternal will without change in the divine essence.

Key Terms
قديم (qadim)
حادث (hadith)
مرجح (murajjih)
إمكان (imkan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, what happens if no determining factor (murajjih) arises for the world's existence?
A) The world comes into existence by itself.
B) The world remains in pure possibility and does not exist.
C) The eternal changes its essence.
D) The philosophers' claim is proven correct.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' position leads to an infinite regress when explaining the origin of a temporal event from an eternal being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believe that God is absolutely unchanging, how do you explain the fact that you are reading this right now? Did God will your reading from eternity? Why did He will it at this moment and not a thousand years ago? The philosophers claimed that an eternal will is sufficient, but Al-Ghazali shows that without a change, there is no explanation. So, do you find yourself relying on a silent assumption that God simply 'chose' a time, without considering the logical implications? Reflect: Is your understanding of God's will consistent with His timelessness? Or are you, like the philosophers, taking His choice for granted? Write a short prayer asking God to grant you certainty in His wisdom, even when logic seems to point to a dilemma.
?
You have likely heard that God created the world 'in time.' But this passage forces you to confront a deep question: if God is eternal and His will is eternal, what made Him decide to create at the moment He did? Can you honestly answer with 'He just did'? If that answer satisfies you, does it also satisfy the philosophers' challenge? Or do you see the need for a deeper explanation—one that goes beyond mere assertion? Write down your honest intellectual struggle, and then ask yourself: How does this affect your trust in God's perfect wisdom and power?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
The Problem of Will and Infinite Regress
Al-Ghazali deconstructs the will-based explanation leading to infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's argument that attributing the world's temporal creation to a new will in God leads to an infinite regress of wills.

Core Idea
A new will in the eternal would itself be a temporal event requiring explanation.

Al-Ghazali deepens the analysis by asking why the world occurred at a specific time. He rejects explanations like inability, impossibility, new purpose, or instrument. The only plausible answer is a new will, but that will itself is a temporal event, leading to an infinite chain. This lesson examines that critical move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the rejected explanations
Al-Ghazali lists several explanations for why the world did not occur earlier: inability, impossibility, purpose, instrument. Note why each is rejected.
Each rejection implies a change in the eternal, which is impossible.
2
Focus on the will explanation
The only remaining explanation is that God did not will the world before. But then a new will must arise. Ask: does this will exist in God's essence or not? Either leads to problems.
3
Trace the infinite regress
If the new will itself requires a prior will, we get an infinite chain. Al-Ghazali says 'the same problem returns' for each will.
This is a classic argument against the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول قولهم يستحيل صدور حادث من قديم مطلقاً ، لأنا إذا فرضنا القديم ولم يصدر منه العالم مثلا ، فإنما لم يصدر لأنه لم يكن للوجود مرجح ، بل كان وجود العالم ممكناً إمكاناً صرفاً ، فإذا حدث بعد ذلك لم يخل ، إما أن يتجدد مرجح ، أو لم يتجدد ؛ فإن لم يتجدد مرجح ، بقى العالم على الإمكان الصرف ، كما كان قبل ذلك ؛ وإن تجدد مرجح فمن محدث ذلك المرجح ؟ ، ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث من قبل ؟ ، والسؤال في حدوث المرجح قائم . بالجملة فأحوال القديم إذا كانت متشابهة ، فإما أن لا يوجد عنه شيء يوجد على الدوام ، فأما أن يتميز حال الترك عن حال الشروع وقط ، وإما أن فهو محال • وتحقيقه أن يقال : لم لم يحدث العالم قبل حدوثه ؟ ، لا يمكن أن يحال على عجزه عن الأحداث ، ولا على استحالة الحدوث ، فإن ذلك يؤدى إلى أن ينقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة ، والعالم من الاستحالة إلى الإمكان ، وكلاهما محالان ، ولا يمكن أن يقال : لم يكن قبله غرض ثم تجدد غرض ولا يمكن أن يحال على فقد آلة ثم على وجودها ، بل أقرب ما يتخيل أن يقال : لم يرد وجوده قبل ذلك ؛ فيلزم أن يقال : حصل وجوده لأنه صار مريداً لوجوده بعد أن لم يكن مريداً ، فتكون قد حدثت الإرادة ، وحدوثه في ذاته محال ، لأنه ليس محل الحوادث ، وحدوثه لا في ذاته لا يجعله مريداً ولنترك النظر في محل حدوثه ، أليس الإشكال قائماً في أصل حدوثه ؟ ! وأنه من ؟! أين حدث ؟ ! ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبله ؟ ! أحدث الآن لا من جهة الله ؟ ! فإن جاز حادث من غير محدث ، فليكن العالم حادثاً لا صانع له ، وإلا فأى فرق بين حادث وحادث ؟ ! و إن حدث بإحداث الله ، فلم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبل ؟ ! ألعدم آلة ، أو قدرة ، أو غرض ، أو طبيعة . فلما أن تبدل ذلك بالوجود حدث ؟ ! عاد الإشكال بعينه . أو لعدم الإرادة ؟ ! فتفتقر الإرادة إلى إرادة وكذا الإرادة الأولى ، ويتسلسل إلى غير نهاية . فإذن قد تحقق بالقول المطلق أن صدور الحادث من القديم من غير تغير أمر من القديم في قدرة أو آلة أو وقت أو غرض، أو طبع ؛ محال ، وتقدير تغير حال محال ، لأن الكلام فى ذلك التغير الحادث كالكلام في غيره تنبيه : فما أقبح ما يقال : من أن الأمور العالية ، تحاول أن تفعل شيئاً لما تحتها لأن ذلك أحسن بها ، ولتكون فعالة للجميل ، أو أن الأول الحق يفعل شيئاً لأجل شيء ، وأن لفعله لمية .

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's will is eternal and unchanging, yet the world is temporal, which al-Ghazali shows is contradictory without a new will.
Correction: Al-Ghazali argues that if God's will is eternal, the world should be eternal; if temporal, then a new will must arise, which leads to infinite regress or change in God.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, why cannot the world's delay be attributed to God's inability or the world's impossibility?
A) Because that would imply a change in God from incapacity to power, and in the world from impossibility to possibility.
B) Because God is all-powerful and the world is always possible.
C) Because inability and impossibility are the same thing.
D) Because the philosophers reject such explanations.

Key Takeaway
Attributing the world's temporal creation to a new will in God leads to an infinite regress of wills, making the philosophers' position untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is not subject to change as this lesson demonstrates, how does that challenge your own sense of what it means to 'want' something? Do you ever assume that God must 'change His mind' to answer your prayers? This lesson forces you to reconsider: is your concept of God's will truly free from temporal succession? Will you commit to examining your own assumptions when you next pray?
?
When you reflect on the fact that the world's existence depends on an eternal will without any new motivation, does that make you feel secure or unsettled? Why? And how does that affect your trust in God's decree, especially in moments of hardship? Can you honestly say you believe that every event in your life comes from a will that never wavers or adapts?
?
Al-Ghazali shows that any new will would require an infinite regress. How does this reframe your understanding of causality? Do you see any area of your life where you rely on a chain of reasons that ultimately must stop? What concrete step can you take today to ground your trust in God as the First Cause, rather than seeking endless explanations?

Conclusion: The Impossibility of Emanation without Change
Al-Ghazali concludes the refutation and warns against purposive explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's final conclusion that emanation of a temporal event from the eternal is impossible without change, and his warning against attributing purpose or 'why' to God's acts.

Core Idea
Emanating a temporal event from the eternal requires change in the eternal, which is impossible.

After dismantling the philosophers' arguments, al-Ghazali delivers his verdict: emanation of a temporal event from an eternal being without any change in the eternal is impossible. He also criticizes the idea that God acts for a purpose or that His act has a 'why'. This lesson captures the final thrust and the moral of the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the conclusion passage
Notice how al-Ghazali summarizes: 'it is established absolutely that the emanation of a temporal event from the eternal without a change... is impossible.'
He lists power, instrument, time, purpose, nature as possible changes.
2
Understand the warning
Al-Ghazali then warns against saying that God acts for the sake of something or that His act has a 'why'. This is a theological correction.
This reflects the Ash'ari view that God's acts are not subject to external purposes.
3
Connect to the larger argument
The entire refutation shows that the philosophers cannot consistently hold both the eternity of God and the temporality of the world without implying change in God.
This is a classic kalam position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول قولهم يستحيل صدور حادث من قديم مطلقاً ، لأنا إذا فرضنا القديم ولم يصدر منه العالم مثلا ، فإنما لم يصدر لأنه لم يكن للوجود مرجح ، بل كان وجود العالم ممكناً إمكاناً صرفاً ، فإذا حدث بعد ذلك لم يخل ، إما أن يتجدد مرجح ، أو لم يتجدد ؛ فإن لم يتجدد مرجح ، بقى العالم على الإمكان الصرف ، كما كان قبل ذلك ؛ وإن تجدد مرجح فمن محدث ذلك المرجح ؟ ، ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث من قبل ؟ ، والسؤال في حدوث المرجح قائم . بالجملة فأحوال القديم إذا كانت متشابهة ، فإما أن لا يوجد عنه شيء يوجد على الدوام ، فأما أن يتميز حال الترك عن حال الشروع وقط ، وإما أن فهو محال • وتحقيقه أن يقال : لم لم يحدث العالم قبل حدوثه ؟ ، لا يمكن أن يحال على عجزه عن الأحداث ، ولا على استحالة الحدوث ، فإن ذلك يؤدى إلى أن ينقلب القديم من العجز إلى القدرة ، والعالم من الاستحالة إلى الإمكان ، وكلاهما محالان ، ولا يمكن أن يقال : لم يكن قبله غرض ثم تجدد غرض ولا يمكن أن يحال على فقد آلة ثم على وجودها ، بل أقرب ما يتخيل أن يقال : لم يرد وجوده قبل ذلك ؛ فيلزم أن يقال : حصل وجوده لأنه صار مريداً لوجوده بعد أن لم يكن مريداً ، فتكون قد حدثت الإرادة ، وحدوثه في ذاته محال ، لأنه ليس محل الحوادث ، وحدوثه لا في ذاته لا يجعله مريداً ولنترك النظر في محل حدوثه ، أليس الإشكال قائماً في أصل حدوثه ؟ ! وأنه من ؟! أين حدث ؟ ! ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبله ؟ ! أحدث الآن لا من جهة الله ؟ ! فإن جاز حادث من غير محدث ، فليكن العالم حادثاً لا صانع له ، وإلا فأى فرق بين حادث وحادث ؟ ! و إن حدث بإحداث الله ، فلم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبل ؟ ! ألعدم آلة ، أو قدرة ، أو غرض ، أو طبيعة . فلما أن تبدل ذلك بالوجود حدث ؟ ! عاد الإشكال بعينه . أو لعدم الإرادة ؟ ! فتفتقر الإرادة إلى إرادة وكذا الإرادة الأولى ، ويتسلسل إلى غير نهاية . فإذن قد تحقق بالقول المطلق أن صدور الحادث من القديم من غير تغير أمر من القديم في قدرة أو آلة أو وقت أو غرض، أو طبع ؛ محال ، وتقدير تغير حال محال ، لأن الكلام فى ذلك التغير الحادث كالكلام في غيره تنبيه : فما أقبح ما يقال : من أن الأمور العالية ، تحاول أن تفعل شيئاً لما تحتها لأن ذلك أحسن بها ، ولتكون فعالة للجميل ، أو أن الأول الحق يفعل شيئاً لأجل شيء ، وأن لفعله لمية .
The first [argument]: Their saying that it is impossible for a temporal event to proceed from the eternal at all. For if we suppose the eternal and the world, for example, did not proceed from it, then it did not proceed only because there was no determining factor (murajjih) for existence, rather the world's existence was pure possibility. Then when it occurred afterwards, it cannot be but that either a determining factor arises or does not arise. If no determining factor arises, the world remains in pure possibility as it was before. If a determining factor arises, then who originated that determining factor? And why did it occur now and not before? The question about the occurrence of the determining factor remains. In sum, if the states of the eternal are similar, then either nothing proceeds from it at all, or it proceeds perpetually. But distinguishing between the state of non-occurrence and the state of initiation is impossible. Its verification is to say: Why did the world not occur before its occurrence? It cannot be attributed to His inability to originate, nor to the impossibility of occurrence, for that would lead to the eternal changing from incapacity to power, and the world from impossibility to possibility, both of which are impossible. Nor can it be said that there was no purpose before and then a purpose arose, nor can it be attributed to the lack of an instrument and then its existence. Rather, the closest thing one might imagine is to say: He did not will its existence before. Then it necessarily follows that its existence occurred because He became willing of its existence after not being willing, so that the will (irada) would have occurred. Its occurrence in His essence is impossible because He is not a locus for temporal events, and its occurrence not in His essence does not make Him willing. Let us leave aside the consideration of its locus; is the problem not established in the very occurrence of the will? And from whom? Where did it occur? Why did it occur now and not before? Did it occur now from no direction of God? For if a temporal event is possible without an originator, then let the world be temporal without a Maker; else what difference is there between one temporal event and another? And if it occurs by God's causing-to-occur, why did it occur now and not before? Was it due to the absence of an instrument, or power, or purpose, or nature? When that changed to existence, it occurred? The same problem returns. Or due to the absence of will? Then the will would require another will, and so the first will, ad infinitum. So it is established absolutely that the emanation of a temporal event from the eternal without a change in the eternal in power, or instrument, or time, or purpose, or nature is impossible, and the assumption of a change in state is impossible, because the discussion about that temporal change is like the discussion about other than it. A reminder: How ugly it is to say that the lofty things try to do something for the sake of what is below them because that is better for them and so that they may be doers of the beautiful, or that the First Truth does something for the sake of something, and that His act has a 'why'.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by Imam al-Ghazali of the philosophers' claim that a temporal event (hadith) cannot emanate from an eternal being (qadim) at all. Al-Ghazali begins by presenting the core of their argument: if we suppose the eternal (God) and the world did not proceed from Him, then the world's existence was purely possible (imkan mahd) with no determining factor (murajjih). If later the world comes into existence, either a determining factor arises or it does not. If it does not arise, the world would remain in pure possibility, so no existence. If a determining factor does arise, then we ask: what originated that determining factor? And why now and not before? The same question applies to the determining factor itself, leading to an infinite regress. This is the first dilemma. Al-Ghazali then sharpens the argument: if the eternal's states are all similar (i.e., no change in essence or attributes), then either nothing proceeds from Him ever, or something proceeds perpetually—but distinguishing a moment of creation from a prior state of non-creation would imply a change in the eternal, which is impossible. He then deepens the analysis by asking why the world did not occur earlier. It cannot be due to God's inability (for that would imply change from incapacity to power) nor due to the impossibility of the world's existence (for that would imply a change from impossibility to possibility). Both are absurd. Nor can it be attributed to a new purpose or instrument arising in God, for that too implies change. The only plausible response is that God did not will the world's existence before. But then we ask: was His will eternal or temporal? If temporal, then the will itself is a temporal event that needs an originator—leading to an infinite regress of wills. If eternal, then the world should have existed eternally, contradicting its temporality. Al-Ghazali then makes a crucial point: if a temporal event can occur without an originator, then the world itself could be temporal without a Maker—which the philosophers deny. But if the world occurs by God's causing-to-occur (ihdath), then why now and not earlier? If due to the absence of an instrument, power, purpose, or nature, then when those are supplied, the same problem returns. If due to the absence of will, then will requires another will ad infinitum. Thus, the philosophers' position leads to an infinite regress or to change in the eternal—both impossible. The passage concludes with a warning against misguided justifications that say the lofty (i.e., God) acts for the sake of something else, or that His act has a 'why', which compromises divine transcendence. This is a classic kalam argument for the necessity of a temporal creation by an eternal will without change in the divine essence.

Key Terms
قديم (qadim)
حادث (hadith)
تغير (taghayyur)
غرض (gharad)
لمية (limiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God creates for a purpose, like making the world perfect or benefiting creatures.
Correction: Al-Ghazali considers such ideas 'ugly' because they imply need or deficiency in God; God's acts are not for external ends.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, what is required for a temporal event to emanate from the eternal?
A) A change in the eternal in power, instrument, time, purpose, or nature.
B) No change at all.
C) An external agent.
D) The temporal event must be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' claim that a temporal event can emanate from the eternal without change is impossible, and attributing a 'why' to God's act is inappropriate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking that God 'must' do something because it makes sense to you? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what would it take for you to surrender your expectations of how God should act?
?
When you pray, do you sometimes feel that God should answer because you have a good reason? How does al-Ghazali's warning against a 'why' for God's act affect your expectation, and can you truly accept that God's will has no external purpose?
?
Reflect on a time when you tried to justify God's actions to someone else using human logic. How might this lesson change your approach, and are you willing to say 'I do not know why, but He is God' without needing a reason?

The Impossibility of a New Will in the Eternal
Ghazali argues against a new will arising in the eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that a new will cannot originate in the eternal being without leading to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
An eternal being cannot change or acquire a new attribute like will.

In this passage, Ghazali begins his refutation by focusing on the nature of divine will. The philosophers claimed that the world could be eternal, but Ghazali shows that their assumption leads to absurd conclusions about God's will. Let's trace his logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the rhythm of Ghazali's argument.
Pay special attention to the rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the core problem with divine will
Ghazali begins with the assumption that God was not willing and then became willing. He shows this would require a new will in God, which is impossible because God is not a locus for events.
Even if the will occurs outside God's essence, it does not make Him actually willing.
3
Understand the question of 'why now'
Ghazali shifts focus to the event itself: why did it occur now and not earlier? He considers several possibilities for the delay: absence of instrument, power, purpose, nature, or will.
Each possibility either leads back to the same problem or to an infinite regress.
4
Trace the infinite regress argument
If the delay was due to absence of will, then the will itself would need another will to arise, and so on without end. This is the infinite regress (tasalsul) that the philosophers wanted to avoid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد أن لم يكن مريداً، فتكون قد حدثت الإرادة، وحدوثه في ذاته محال، لأنه ليس محل الحوادث، وحدوثه لا في ذاته لا يجعله مريداً. ولنترك النظر في محل حدوثه، أليس الإشكال قائماً في أصل حدوثه؟ وأنه من؟ أين حدث؟ ولم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبله؟ أحدث الآن لا من جهة الله؟ فإن جاز حادث من غير محدث، فليكن العالم حادثاً لا صانع له، وإلا فأي فرق بين حادث وحادث؟ وإن حدث بإحداث الله، فلم حدث الآن ولم يحدث قبل؟ ألعدم آلة، أو قدرة، أو غرض، أو طبيعة. فلما أن تبدل ذلك بالوجود حدث؟ عاد الإشكال بعينه. أو لعدم الإرادة؟ فتفتقر الإرادة إلى إرادة وكذا الإرادة الأولى، ويتسلسل إلى غير نهاية. فإذن قد تحقق بالقول المطلق أن صدور الحادث من القديم من غير تغير أمر من القديم في قدرة أو آلة أو وقت أو غرض أو طبع محال، وتقدير تغير حال محال، لأن الكلام في ذلك التغير الحادث كالكلام في غيره. تنبيه: فما أقبح ما يقال من أن الأمور العالية تحاول أن تفعل شيئاً لما تحتها لأن ذلك أحسن بها، ولتكون فعالة للجميل، أو أن الأول الحق يفعل شيئاً لأجل شيء، وأن لفعله لمية. والكل محال، ومهما كان العالم موجوداً واستحال حدوثه، ثبت قدمه لا محالة.
After it was not willing, then will would have occurred, and its occurrence in His essence is impossible, because He is not a locus for events, and its occurrence not in His essence does not make Him willing. Let us leave aside considering the locus of its occurrence: is not the problem standing in the very fact of its occurrence? And where did it occur? And why did it occur now and not occur before? Did it occur now from no direction of God? If an event is permissible without an originator, then let the world be an event without a maker, otherwise what difference between one event and another? And if it occurred by God's causing it to occur, then why did it occur now and not occur before? Was it due to absence of an instrument, or power, or purpose, or nature? So when that changed to existence it occurred? The same problem returns. Or due to absence of will? Then will would need another will, and likewise the first will, and it would regress infinitely. Thus it is verified absolutely that the emanation of the event from the eternal without a change in something of the eternal—in power, instrument, time, purpose, or nature—is impossible, and positing a change of state is impossible, because the discourse about that new change is the same as the discourse about other than it. A notice: how ugly is what is said: that high things strive to do something for what is below them because that is better for them, and so that they might be doers of the beautiful, or that the First Truth does something for the sake of something, and that His act has a 'why'. And all of that is impossible. And as long as the world exists and its coming to be is impossible, its eternity is established without doubt.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents Ghazali's refutation of the philosophers' argument that the world must be eternal because a new event (like creation) cannot originate from an eternal being without change. He begins by considering the problem of divine will: if God was not willing and then became willing, then a new will occurred in Him, which is impossible because He is not a subject for accidents. Even if the will occurs outside His essence, that does not make Him truly willing. Ghazali then says to set aside the locus and focus on the very occurrence of the event. He poses a series of rhetorical questions: where did it occur? Why now and not earlier? If it can happen without a cause, then the world needs no maker; if it happens by God's causing, why now? He lists possible reasons: absence of instrument, power, purpose, or nature. If these were absent before and then present, the same problem remains. If it is due to absence of will, then will itself would need another will, leading to an infinite regress. So the conclusion is that it is absolutely impossible for a new event to proceed from the eternal without a change in something like power, instrument, time, purpose, or nature. Positing a change in the eternal state is also impossible, as the same problem applies to that change. Then Ghazali adds a sharp notice ('tanbih'): it is ugly to say that high entities strive for what is below them for beauty's sake, or that the First Truth acts for a purpose, because that implies a 'why' for His act. All such explanations are impossible. Finally, he restates the core: if the world exists and its origination is impossible, then its eternity is necessarily proven. Note: This argument is the philosophers' own proof, which Ghazali here presents and deconstructs to show its flaws; he is not agreeing with their conclusion but rather showing that their reasoning leads to absurdities.

Key Terms
الإرادة (al-irada: will)
القديم (al-qadim: the eternal)
الحادث (al-hadith: the event/incident)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul: infinite regress)
المحال (al-muhal: the impossible)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Ghazali is proving the eternity of the world here.
Correction: Ghazali is actually showing that the philosophers' own argument for eternity leads to absurdities, thereby undermining it. He is not endorsing eternity.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what happens if the delay of the event is attributed to absence of will?
A) The will arises without need for another will.
B) The will would need another will, leading to an infinite regress.
C) The event occurs immediately without any cause.
D) The absence is due to a change in God's power.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' assumption that a new event can arise from an eternal being without change leads to the absurdity of an infinite regress of wills.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you beg Allah in du'a for something you desperately want, do you sometimes feel that your persistence might 'change His mind'? How does Ghazali's logical proof that a new will cannot arise in the Eternal strike your heart? What does this mean for how you should understand the timing of His response? Will you trust His eternal will even when it delays?
?
Think of a moment when you regretted something that happened and wished it could be undone. If Allah's will cannot change, then that event was always part of His eternal decree. Does this bring you comfort or discomfort? Are you willing to submit to the fact that everything—even your pain—was eternally willed for you? What would change in your heart if you truly believed this?
?
Ghazali shows that the philosophers' assumption that God can will a temporal creation without change collapses under logical scrutiny. But what about your own assumptions? Have you ever thought that you could 'earn' or 'deserve' something from Allah in a way that forces His will to respond? How does this passage expose that as a form of entitlement? Repent and realign your heart to see everything as a pure gift from an unchanging Will.
